commitment may weaken andprogresstoward reformmay slip inthe course ofpolitical
compromise. It pointed to lengthy stakeholder consultations during preparation of the GPAL as
one strategy used to managethis risk.Another element of the risk mitigationstrategy was to
await the implementation of a significant portionof the Borrower's reformprogram before
presenting the GPAL for Boardapproval. Managementbelieves that the treatment ofrisk
provided the Executive Directors with adequateinformationfor consideration intheir decisions
onthe proposed GPAL.

INADEQUATEATTENTION TO THE RISKOFPOORFORESTMANAGEMENT

        "Forest management is sopoor as to cause actual harm to theforests. TheBank made
       the loan knowing that the State had no effective ability toprotect theforests of the
       Claimants through the implementation of managementpolicies or practices onjagile
       forests, 10% conservation set-asides, rotation cycles. There is no `National Forest Plan'.
       This was a riskfor the Bank. ''                       [Request, Subsection 5.131

        "In our submission, the State does not have the ability to manage and conserve the
       rainforests in the country.I'                         [Request, Subsection 5.251

                                                  25


RESPONSE

75.     Good quality national level forest information is available through the PapuaNewGuinea
Forest InformationMapping System, andthe IRT noted inits report that this i s an excellent tool
for sectoral and project-level planning. The IRT further notedthat Forest Authority staff were
able to use this data base to produceproject level maps and area information, of sufficient quality
to allow estimates of net loggable area to bemade. There is a strong technical argument that the
priority inPapuaNewGuinea be on building capacity to produce good field inventories for
forest areas being consideredfor logging, upon which sustainablecut estimates can be based.
This is a different form of inventory from national level inventory. The IRT recommendedthat a
national forest plan should be developed from an updating of provinciallevel forest management
plans,jointly preparedby the Provinces, the ForestAuthority andthe Office ofEnvironment and
Conservation. Insupport of this arrangement, the IRT suggestedthat clear directions be
formulated to guide the development of cutting cycles at the FMA level, and that these must
include provision for conservation set-asides and also be subject to initial environmental
assessment.

76.     The IRT did notethat inits view the sustainedtimber yield principle has beenstrongly
adoptedby the Forest Authority as the basis for planning forest operations, andthat it also
figures significantly inForestry Board deliberations.

77.     The Sustainable Forest Managementcomponent of the FCP is focused on the priority
tasks that need to be completed to improve sustainability. There is ample scope withinthis
component to assist the Borrower inthe development of the analytical andprocedural elements
referred to inthe Request and inthe IRT's recommendations, and the Bank will engage the
Borrower indiscussionsonthis issue during the course o f implementation of the FCP.

INADEQUATE SUPPORT FORCOMMUNITY FORESTRY

        A sub-section of thepresentation on harm states: "It is unfortunate that methods of forest
        utilization that assistpeople to control their own development, such as community
        forestry are not well supported by the Bank, the State, or the Papua New Guinea Forest
        Authority.... Communityforestry conforms with Bankpolicy, see OP 4.36.... The
        Claimants have never been assisted by the State toparticipate in communityforestry ...
        [therefore] the State is in breach of thesepolicies. [Request, Subsection 5.IO]
                                                                  "




RESPONSE

79.     As discussed inpara. 24, the GPAL focused on implementing key structural reforms in
the forestry sector. Itdid not finance any specific forestry investments as structural adjustment
loans are not intendedto provide this type o f support. However, now that the governance reforms
inthe forestry sector havebeenputinplace, the FCPwill support arange ofspecific forestry
investments, including community forestry activities. More thanhalfo fthe total proceeds o f the
FCP will be directedtowards the empowerment o f landowners to organize, decide and negotiate
the use o f their resources, andto provide financing for landowners interested indeveloping their
own sustainable resource projects: under the FCP (Annex C) communities that wish to make
investments inforest projects on their land, and those that seek to assist them inthis, will be
eligible to apply to the ConservationTrust Fundfor support to do so. Moreover, communities
will benefit directly from activities the Borrower will initiate withthe assistance o fthe
Landowner Forest Decision Makingcomponent o f the project, which will support the formation
o f effective landowner representative groups, and develop knowledge andtraining on forest
issues among those groups.

80.     As a complement to these efforts, the Australian Agency for International Development
(AusAID) remains engaged inthe PapuaNew Guinea forest sector andhas expressed interest in
working on aspects o f community forestry there. It will also support the continuation o f the
National Forest ConservationAction Program, which has supported many activities aimed at
developing community involvement with forests inthe past, and will continue to do so. The
EuropeanCommission also has a program operative inPapuaNew Guinea at present which
focuses on community forestry.

           ` I , . .but, most importantly, for thepurposes of this submission: an industry whose sales
                    revenue is less than its out-goings, an industry that is uneconomic.
         "The uneconomic nature of the logging industry has been apparentfor some time.
        Logging could only bejustified in very narrowproft-and-loss terms,fFom thepoint of
        view of an export logger. In terms of real economy, externalities were never taken into
        account. However, now prices are low, the industry is uneconomic, even in a narrow

        economic impact upon its economy of an activity.         "  [Request, Section 2,p. 61

         "Thepolicy mandate in OP 4.36 of sustainable managementof naturalforests is
        problematic in Papua New Guinea's mixed-speciesforests. Theevidencepoints to
         industrial scale sustainableforestry not being either economically or ecologically
        feasible.  "Reasons given inthe Request are that the cost o f restoring the forest to its
         original condition i s very high; selective logging on an industrial scale tends to killoff
         highvalue, slow-growing hardwoods; logging companies do not observe the Logging
         Code o f Conduct and often manage to clearcut their concessions; and mortality o f 53 to
         79 percent o fthe trees left standingafter selective logging has been reportedinPapua
         New Guinea.                                            [Request, Subsections5.14 -5.241

REsPoNsE

81.      The Request makes broadassertions as to the economic viability o f logging inPapua
New Guinea's rainforests, the general feasibility o f sustainable forest management intropical
forests, and issues related to appropriate cutting cycles, selective logging and stand damage.
These questions relate to complex analytical issues that are presented indetail inAnnex M.As
far as the economic argument is concerned, the potential viability o fthe logging sector cannot be
judged on the basis o f its performance under conditions prevailing inthe immediatepast. It is in
the nature o f the logging sector for the market to be volatile, and its long-term viability will
depend on the overall trends inboth costs and prices. There is no basis for judgingthe direction
o f either on the evidence available at the present time. The role o f government, inthis situation,
i s to ensure that reasonable economic rent andreturns to landowners are gleaned from the sector,
andthat the broadvalues inherent inthe forest are protected andmaintained.

82.      Logs have value on the international market and it is evident that pressure to utilize
forests to produce them will remain strong inPapuaNew Guinea as elsewhere. Under these
circumstances, the real choice available is not betweenutilization o fthe forests for logging,
among other uses, or large scale withdrawal o f forests from this form o f use. Rather the choice is
betweenwhether utilization for logs is carried out with due regardto the sustainability, the
protection o fvital areas andthe important externalities o f forests, or whether it is done
destructively and unsustainably.

83.      Annex Mdiscusses some recent work that has been carried out on the general subject o f
sustainability intropical forests. It is clear that sustainable management o f tropical forests is not
only feasible, but that key operational techniques to achieve it have been well knownfor many
decades. The problem has beenthat there have been few large-scale attempts to implement these,
because o f the financial attractiveness o fhighly exploitive andnon-sustainable operations in
situations where poor governance and capacity problems permit this to occur. The challenge for
PapuaNew Guinea i s to develop the means to implement sustainable management effectively. In
the view ofthe Bank, the sameproblems o f governance, capacity weakness andinstitutional
failure that make implementation o f sustainable forestry a difficult task also apply to all proposed
alternatives to sustainable management under selective logging. Unless appropriate measures -
such as enhanced monitoring, enforcement and participation by all interest groups inresource
decision making- are implementedto address perverse incentives andvested interests,
governance issues and unsustainable forestry are likely to prevail inPapuaNew Guinea. Taken
together the GPAL and the FCP constitute a serious effort by the Borrower, the Bank and other
donors to address governance problems inthe forestry sector inPapuaNew Guinea, and to

                                              28


support efforts to implementactivities that empower communities and promote greater
sustainability.

                                                                                          25th August 2000

         re. follow up to the meetingwith Greenpeace Australia Pacific, Sydney,
         August 15.
-        Dear Mr. Rohizid,

         Thank you ior the meetingon 15 August 2000. Followingis a summary of the main
         points of the meeting,and our recommendationsas a result of that discussion. We
         lookforward10 hearingfrom you on any progress on these points.

         The Moratorium: We are inagreement that the moratoriumis welcomedby a
         diverse rangeoi stakeholders,includingthe PrimeMinisterof PNG, the World Bank
         and Greenpeaceas a sound andfar-sighted policy instrument. Further,we are
         agreed that the moratoriumis necessaryto achieve meaningful reforminthe
         forestry sector and assist broadergovernanceissues in PNG.


         The Reviewof the Forestryconcessions: Achievingthe necessaryreformswill,
         as the Bank has correctlyassertedin its SAL and FCP loanconditions, require a
         comprehensivereviewof proposedAND existing logging concessions.However, it
         will also requirebuildinglandholdercapacity, creating greater transparencyand
         accountability,establishingconstraint-based land useplanningsystem,
         transformingihe cutture (role/structure/function)of the ForestAuthority, investingin
         services and community-basedalternativeland uses, and conservingor preventing
         industrialloggingin several key areas.

a    Greenpeaceis deeplyconcemedthat the reviewplanned by the World Bank will
     only consider new loggingprojects.Shouldany of the new projectscommence
     beforean adequate reviewof the concessionscurrently heldby potential tenderers,
     there is a real likelihoodthat irreparableharmwill be causedto the property of
     customary landowners.The poor forest managementand conservationrecordof
     loggingcompaniescurrentlyoperating in PNGwould lead to the errors of the past
     being replicatedintothe future. As the Bank is well aware, there is no equitable
     revenuesystem in place, and customarylandowners will continue to be exploited
     under a repetitionof existing arrangements.


     SAL Disbursement: Inyour letter of July 7,and in our meeting,you had statedthat
     it is essentialthat only those actionsthat a Governmentcan comply with duringthe
     periodof the loanare required. In particular, you stated, despitethe Second
     Trancheconditionalitythat there will be a reviewof proposedand existing logging
     concessions:


     "itwouldnot be possible to review allprojects whicharepresentiy operatingin PNG
     in the time frame of the SAL'.


     Our understandingis that the loan is for twenty years, which should give ample time
     for a full review of all existinglogging operations.Therefore, hilewe appreciate the
    .constraintsofthe SAL, Greenpeaceis concernedit could constitutean
     inappropriateuse of publicmoneyto disburse funds to PNG'sgovemmentwithout
     concreteassurancesthat the moratorium will stay in place until both phases of the
     review havebeencompleted, its recommendationsimplemented,and a majority of
     the fundamental changes mentioned above are achieved.




     Breaches of Loan Conditions: As we outlined in the meeting,the Forest Authority
     has beenactingin a renegadefashion, ignoringthe moratoriumand continuingto
     preparefast track projects.The KamulaDoso FMA inthe Westem Province and the
     Amanab Block1-4 FMAs are on track to beingallocatedin spite of the current
     moratorium.The danger here is that the ForestAuthority will drift into enforceable
     contractualrslationshipsand circumvent publiclaw checks and balances.

     The SecondTrancheconditionalitystates:

     "Comp!eteindependentreview of all FMAs, timberpermits and geographic
     extensionsto timberpermits"

     Le., that the moratoriummust remainuntila review of proposedana EXISTING
     loggingconcessionsis completed.A thorough review is requiredto effect genuine
     reforminthe sector, and this may requirean extensionto the moratorium.

    Further,as we mentionedinthe meeting, despiteyour letter to the PNG
    Government,we understandthat the problemwith the Kiunga-Aeanbakroad
    remains. We havebeentoldthat the Minister of Forestshas approvedan extension
    to this project.We know that this is of critical concernto the World Bank.
    Greenpeace has beenunableto meet with the Minister and clarifythis issue. The
    Minister recently failedto attend a scheduledmeetingwith the PapuaNew Guinean
    NGO's to discuss this issue.


    Given the above, Greenpeace's position is:


    e we would not actively oppose disbursement of the second tranche before
        the review is finished IFthe above projects are stopped;
    a the PrimeMinister states publicly that the moratorium will stay in place
        untilthe review of all projects, proposed and existing, isfinished; and
    a   its recommendationsare implemented (Le. that ongoing mechanisms are in
        placeto ensurethat the laws are being followed).


    Transparency and Participation inthe Review:



a   We also discussed several recommendationsfor increasedtransparencyand public
    participationinthe first phaseof the review (Le. of the proposed "fasttrack"
    concessions).We suggestedthat:

    0   a civil society/NGO representativeshouldbe includedon the committee that
        overseesthe review processand results (notethat Eco-ForestryForum has
        nominatedKelly Kallit):
    e   an experton publicparticipationlinformationdissemination be included as part of
        the phase 1 review team (notethat Eco-ForestryForum has nominated Paul
        Chatterton)I
    0   the reviewfindings be made publicand that a public comment period and/or
        forum beincludedinthe review process (notethat organisingthis would be the
        role of the public participationexperton the review team):

    The review process set out clear obligations to implement recommendations and
    establisha l&nq/ongoing review mechanismto ensure that:

    0   "due diligence' is appliedand met
    0   problemsuncoveredare fixed
    0   projectsa e subject to ongoingassessmentprocess which guarantees
        compliancewith legal requirements.

    It shouldbe notedthat severalconcessionsproposedover biologically critical areas
    or wherethere is localoppositionto industriallogging   - e.g. KamulaDoso,Amanab
    1-4, Laks Muny 1-2,CollingwoodBay, Musa Pongani, Hunstein Ranges should   -
    not be allocatedfor industrialloggingland use. WWF, in particular, is concemed

.-


     over the Wildlife ManagementArea it assistedin establishingover the Hunstein
     Ranges.This area of highbiodiversitypriorityis inthe April-SalumeiFMA. We need
     to guarantee that the April Salumei FMA is not put up for tendering]andthe
     Hunstein Ranges and associatedlandsthreatened.



     in our meeting,you agreedthat these recommendationswere sound and that the
     Bank would includethem in its reply to the GOPNG'sTerms of Reference for phase
     1of the review(proposedprojects).You also assured us that the Bank wouldstress
    that the reviewteam conductfield visits to check on the validity of acquisition
     proceduresas well as conductstudies in existingconcessionsas requiredfor
     assessing 'due diligence"of potential bidders.


    Supportto the PNG Governmentin recognition of revenueforgone: As we
     discussed, atiroroughreformof the forest industrywill take years, and is best
     accomplisiCIedin the context of a moratoriumon new operations. If the Government
     is to follow this course, it will haveto resist significantpressuresfrom nationaland
     provincialpoliticiansl landowners,and logging companies seeking new operations.
     One factor that may helpthe governmentto holdto the long coursewould be new
     and additionaifunding, with the greater proportiontargeted at localgovemment
     servias and landownersin areas coveredby the moratorium. Greenpeace
     understandsthat the Bank may not be in a positionto providesuch funds, but the
     Bank could play a role in describingthe pressureson the PNG Governmentto
    funding agencies,andthe value of grantsthat can be seen to be replacingforgone
     revenue. Any commentsor advice on this pointwould be appreckted.


    The Prime Minister'svisit to Washington DC: Thank you for informingus of the
    upcominsvisit of Prime Ministerto Washington, and his plannedmeeting with
    World Bank PresidentWolfensohn.It would be valuable if the briefingnotes for
    Wolfensohncould includereferenceto the Banks belief in the value to PNG of the
    moratoriumsaying in place, bothto improvegovernance]and to effect a thorough
    reviewand reformof the ForestAuthority. Greenpeacebelievesthis is an ideal
    opportuniv to encouragethe PrimeMinister to confirm his support for this
    approachpublicly,to allay our fears that as soon as the SecondTranche is
    distributed, loggingwill quicklyexpandinto unallocated areas.

    Yours faithfulti,.

    Brian Brunton

                                including an extract containing a description o f the timber
                                area, the name o f the permit or authority holder, the permit
                                or authority number and the duration o f the permit or
                                authority;    2nd
                                    (x) forest potential areas including an extract containing
                                        their details ana the unailocated areas;   and
                                   (xi) Forest Management Agreements and field reports
                                        relating to tlie signing of the Agreements with
                                        resource owners.

                     (4)   A person may, on payment of a prescribed fee and at such times
                  as are appointed by the Authority search the Public Register, and, on the
                  payment of a prescribed fee, obtain copies of any document or copies of
                  any entry made inthe Public Register.".

11. NEW SECTION 144.
    The Principal Act is amended in Part X by inserting after Section 143 the following:-

                          Subject to Section 90D(23), a timber authority that is valid and in force
                immediately before the coining iiiio operation of this provision shail, on tliat
                corning iiiio operation. have i d 1 force and effcci for the duration or its term.".

LETTERFROMBANK COUNTRY DIRECTOR TO PRIME MINISTER
                 OF 16 JULY 2000 ON
    PROPOSED EXTENSION OFAIAMBAK ROAD PROJECT


     ;AN. 1E. 2002   3 37FiY     'YClRSD 3ANK E A 3 I P 202 5 2 2        137:


                                                         Levd la, CML auildlng
                                                         TheWorld Bank
                                                            14kdpwn Plaw
                                                          Sydney, NSWPO(M
L                                                            AUSfRALlA




                                                                             July 16,2000


              Hon. Sir MekereMorauta, Kt,MF'
              Prime Minister o f PapuaNew Guinea and
              Minister for FinanceandTreasury
              Department of Prime Minister,NationalParliament
              P.O. Box639
              Waigani, NCD
              PAPUA NEWGUINEA

              DearMr.PrimeMinister:

                      We understandthat your Cabinet is'likelyto consider a co-submission next week
              from the Transport, Agriculture, Works, and Forests Ministers seeking a massive
              extension to the Kiunga-Aimbakroad project, consisting of a 6 kilometre wide corridor
              for 240 km in stage 2, and 635 km in stage 3. Basically the (so-called) roads would
..-.          stretch all round Western Province on the eastern side o f the Fly river (Wawoi Falls,
              downto Musumunguon the Fly river, up to Nomad, down to Levame, on to Cassowary,
              up to Drimgas, another loop to the refugee camp area, etc), and ultimately to Kikori in
              GulfProvince, etc.

                     This extension is likely not in line with your stated intentions for the forestry
              sector and the Loan Agreement betweenthe World Bpmk and the Government of Papua
              New Guinea. Inview of its importancefor the implementation of your reform program, I
              would like to propose that a decision on the matter be postponed until we have time to
              jointly examinethe matter thoroughly.


                                                                             Sincerelyyours,




                                                                             KlausRohIand


              cc: - H.E. NagoraBogan
                    TheAmbassador ofPapaNew Guineato theUnitedStates

  1     FOLLOW UP ACTION PLAN FOLLOWING INDEPENDENT REVIEW OF                                      '

  I                             PROPOSEDFOREST PROJECTS


   The following Plan of Actions. and implementation schedule for those actions. !vas approved
   by the National Executive Council on I4"' Uovemoer 200 I under Decision No. l88/200 1.
   The Decision was based upon the recommendationso ithe indeDendent Review of Proposed
   Forest Projects. feedback t'roin interested stakeholders. and contributions trom the Inter-
   Agency Forestry Review Coinmittee (IAFRCI:       -
1. Policy and General Issues: -

   I.1. The IAFRC is to be retained and expanded. to include representation from the National
        Forest Board. iiidustr!, and non-government organisations. to review the current ( 19901
        National Forest Polic\, and propose revisions. if and tvhere required. to the current
        Policy and ensiling Ie~islation.giving attention to landowner participation in decision
        inakinp and broader iaiduse issues. including rorest conservation policies. community
        forestry and plantation rL>restp. The (.'Jmmitree           -iiould   titilise tlie policy
        recornmendations of tlie Independent Review of Proposed Pro-iects. feedback to their
        report. presentations b? the National Forest Service and other contributions. including
        from a prospective policy itorkshop. Technical support for this process may be
        obtained. if and \\here required. notably under the Forest and Conservation Project. The
        Committee. to be coordinated from CACC. is given until the elid of March 2002 to
        provide its recommendations tor NEC.

   1.2. As part o t the above review. the IAFRC       I\iil examine the proposal for the current
        forestry administration to be further restructured to improve performance and good
        governance. iiicluding the idea ot separating the policy responsibilities from the
        implementation and operational responsibilities.      ith policy being placed potentially
        within a Department ot' Natural Resources or Primary Industry (responsible also for
        policy tor other rural land uses. such as asriculture. and possibly also fisheries] and the
        PNG Forest Authority responsible as the implementation agency. Other proposed
        options. such as separating inspection tiom planning functions may also be examined.
        and the potential for contracting out further tasks. Recommendationsare to be provided.
        as part of the policy exercise (above). by end March 2002.

   I.3. As part of the above review. the IAFRC \\,illexamine the sectoral planning provisions
        of the Foresrr?, Act. and. where appropriate. recommends bv end March 2002.
        mechanisms to rationalise procedures. including the removal o f any inappropriateand/or
        non-effective componentsof the National Forest Plan.

   I.4. TheForestryAct will beamendedto includeaclear statementthattheNationalForest
        Plan is the sum total of the approved Provincial Forest Plans. The Forest Board is to be
        provided greater time to assess and revoke. if required. proposed provincial approvals
        for TAs. Detailed recommendationsand drafting instructions are to be provided, as part
        ofthe policy exercise (above). bvend March 2002.

   1.5. A formal register of genuine eco-forestry and forest conservation (and any similar)
        projects is to be established (and readily accessible to the PNGFA. OEC. and all other
        interestedparties) to include projects where the landowners have indicatedtheir support
        by forming an Incorporated Land Group and entering into a written agreement with an


                                                                                                  1

     NGO. Provincial Government or any other similar party. Projects on the register are to
     be taken into account in Provincial and Nationai Forest Plans. This register should be
     drawn up by the end o f Februarv 2002 at the Forest Authority. based upon material
     provided from OEC and other reievant sources. Support tor its preparation should be
     madeavailable. if necessary. under the forthcoming Forest and Conservation Project.

1.6. In the interest of improved xcountabilit!,. [tie required content of the PNG Forest
     Authority's Annual Report are to be specified b!, Regulation. The required composition
     of the report should be dratied b!, tile PNGFA. in consultation t\ith the Central
     Agencies. and approved b? the Forest Board. before submission to NEC as draft
      Regulations by the end of tlie December 7001, and applicable to the 2001 Report (and
     the outstanding 1997-1_000Reponsi.

1.7. In the interest o t sound plantation forestry management. harvesting and export
     arrangements. plantation torests are to be subject to more appropriate and simpler legal
     and administrative procedures. possibly outside the Forestry Act. The IAFRC will
      promptly review the applicable policy m a legislation      1%ith respect to all plantation
      operations iinciuding tcak. pine. rubberwood and balsa, ana provide recommendations
      for NEC b\.the end ot Februar\ 1002:

1 .EL An independent capacit!' to properly facilitate land group incorporation will be created
      either attached to an elistin? Government Department. or through the use of certified
      private sector individuals or organisations. The IAFRC should exainine this idea further.
      in consultation also  \\i t h the Lands. Xlining and Petroleum and Energy Departments.
      and provide a recommendation for NEC oii its establishment and operation by the end o f
      Februarv 2002. It is envisaged that this entity ivould be supported initially by the
      planned Forest and Conservation Project (FCP).

I.9. The office of the Registrar of Titles nithin the Department of Lands and Physical
      Planning is to be further strengthened to a point where it can properly vet applications
      for incorporated Land Group registration. .-lissistancetor institutional strengthening may
      be provided under the FCP from earlv 2002.

1.10. An assessment is to be inade ot' tlie role forestry projects could play in rural
      development through genuine stakeholder partnerships with landowners. inciuding
      examination o f different inodels of community participation in some existing
      agricultural and other projects (e.g. Fly River Rubber. NBPOL Kulu-Dagi expansion.        `


      etc.). This task can be undertaken as part of a follow up to the current Forest Revenue
      Review. under the FCP. in earlv 2002, including examining improvement to the current
      system of royalties. Project Development Benefits (PDBs). etc.

I.I1. The Independent Review report is to be made a public document by the end of
      November 2001. with copies provided to key institutions, including the National
      Library. Somare Library and other educational and public facilities. and that a workshop

      Authority and OEC staff. sectoral stakehoiders and the public. and to enable wider

    Regarding the Moratorium, tne Mission conveyed the Bank.s
    interpretation o f the Moratorium t o the GOPNG: that no new
    permits o r extensions t o existing permits be granted/approved by
    the National Forest Board. The Mission also recommended that
    NEC issue a public statement of i t s support f e r the Moratorium
    ana Review process.

     (Note: In our previous discussion i n February, the Bank stated
    that issuing such permits or extensions o r issuing permits f o r any
    .exemptions. t o the Moratorium would be interpreted as non-
    compliance/breaches o f the SAP and FCP loan conditions, and
    would result i n h a l t i n g these loans until reversals were made. In
    our conversation today, we did not discuss whether the Bank.s
    interpretation o f the Moratorium includes a r e s t r i c t i o n on
   granting/approving new o r on renewing e x i s t i n g Timber
   Authorities (TAs). We assume that it does include a t least the
    former, but would be g r a t e f u l i f you would c l a r i f y t h i s point.
   Also, we f a i l e d t o discuss whether the Bankss i n t e r p r e t a t i o n o f
    the Moratorium includes any r e s t r i c t i o n s on the acquisition o f
    new areas o r only applies t o the a l l o c a t i o n o f new areas. For
    example, has the Bank conveyed t o GOPNG that acquiring the
    r i g h t s t o new areas by entering into/signing new FMAs
    constitutes a breach o f the Moratorium? We believe that such an
    interpretation i s essential i f the Moratorium i s t o fully achieve i t s
    intended aim of creating space f o r meaningful reform. Without
    redirecting PNGFA energies away from a l l o c a t i n g AND
    acquiring new areas towards improving management o f e x i s t i n g
    ones, there i s a r e a l danger o f sanctioning .business as usual.
    and loosing crucial opportunities afforded by the Moratorium.

1  We would be g r a t e f u l therefore, i f you could c l a r i f y the Bank.s
   p o s i t i o n on t h i s p o i n t . )

   Regarding the Review, the Mission provided the GOPNG w i t h a
   discussion document/draft TOR suggesting elements f o r a TOR
   f o r the Review. The Bank,s p o s i t i o n i s t h a t the Review should
   be conducted by an independent team and t h a t i t be transparent

    INDEPENDENT INSPECTIONTEAM REPORT:
PROJECTREVIEW REPORTONKIUNGA-AIAMBAKROAD,
        POND0 AND TUWAPUPROJECTS


CLAIMED VIOLATIONS OF THE MORATORIUM


                          ClaimedViolations of the iMoratorium

The Request alleges a number o f instances where the moratorium on proceeding with
pending applications has been breached.
Most o fthe cases cited have been discussed in greater detail inthe report of the
Independent Review Team. That report laid out specific measures that needed to be taken
ineachcase, andthe Time BoundAction Planendorses these for implementation by
Government.
Itis apparent that intwo cases. Pondo and Tuwapu, actions were takenwhich resulted in
some logging occurring. Both o f these operaticns were stopped by Government. before
significant volumes o f timber were removed. While there remains some further work to
be done on establishing the facts inthese cases. it appears that they did proceed to some
logging, and that this was inappropriate. On the other hand. it is encouraging that the
system is working well enough to have had these operations terminated relatively soon
after they commenced.
The status o f each of the operations cited inthe request, to the best o f the Bank's
knowledge, is as follows:
        Pondo. Operations inthe project area have beenterminated. subject to
        requirements as recommended by the IRT;
        Tuwapu. Operations by Vanimo Forests Products have beenterminated untilall
        procedures for allocation as stipulated under the Forestry Act are fulfilled.
        East Awin. There is no recent evidence o f new operations within this project
        area. There was illegal encroachment by the Concord Pacific road building
        operation at Aiambak. some 18 months ago.
        Kamula Doso. Operations at this site cannot proceed untilall procedures for the
        application have been completed correctly.
        Amanab Blocks 1to 4. All allocation procedures were suspended untilthe
        moratorium was lifted on 30thNovember 2001.
        Semabo. This project was advertised beforethe imposition o fthe moratorium.
        However, the allocation process was suspended under the moratorium.
        KuluDagi. This project was was exempted fiom the moratorium basedon
        recommendations by the IRT. It had been cleared for oil palmplantation in
        accordance with legislationwhich was current at the time.

    a   Bakada. This is not a new project. Bakaka-Madedua is anexisting Timber
        Permit covered under a a valid Permit. It was without a contract operator for some
        time; one has been hired recent1;y


                        PNG FORESTRY REVIEW TEAM

        AUDITING FORESTRY PROJECTS CURRENTLY "IN PROCESS" FOR
 COMPLIANCE WITH THEREQUIREMENTS OF THEPOLICY, THEFORESTRY ACT
                     AND OTHER REGULATIONS AND GUIDELINES



To:                    Governmentof Papua New Guinea
                       C/- The InteragencyForesuy Review Committee
                       Office of the Chief Secretary to Govemment

From:                  Review Team

Date:                  4 October 2001 (Updated draft of 5 March 2001)

Re:                    INDIVIDUALPROJECT REVIEW REPORTNUMBER31

                       AJAMBAK-KIUNGA ROADTIMBER AUTHORITY
                       (WESTERNPROVINCE)




AUDIT CONCLUSIONS:

RESOURCE ISSUES:

This project is in breach of the National Forest Policy 1991 and the current provisions of
the Forestry Act 1991 (as amended) in that the logging taking place either side of the
road corridor is not reguiated through either a proper Forest ManagementAgreement or
a proper Timber Authority. The project cannot be considered to be a forestry project in
any proper forest management sense. The project is also in breach of the Act in that
logging appears to have moved into the East Awin Forest ManagementAgreement area
without due allocation process being observed.

LEGAL ISSUES:

At no time since the purported issuance of t k Timber Autkrity in April 1994 has any
aspect of due process been observed. This has arisen from matters beyond the direct
control of the PNGFA.

LANDOWNER ISSUES:

There has been no landowner mobiiisation for this project. The holder of the Timber
Authority claims to be a landowner company but is a foreign company (50% foreign
owned). The logging contractor Concord Pacific Ltd continues to pay less royalty than
K10 per cubic meter despite a letter from PNGFA directing the company to pay the
                                                                                        -
Review of "InProcess"Forestry P,?Tiecis
IndividualProjectReport 37 Aiambak-KiungaRoad TA
                             -

 legally mandated rate of K10 per m3 from the beginning of logging. Landowners
 complainof harassment(includingfrom `Police') and threats with firearms.

 RECOMMENDATIONS (INCLUDINGCORRECTIVE MEASURES IF REQUIRED):

    That Court action should be taken forthwith to review the Orders permitting the
    logging operationssince November 1999.

    That any application to extend the scope and term of this Timber Authority be
    soundly rejected.

    That any further application for road line clearing should be properly considered
    under the ForestryAct 1991in light of the Amendments madeto the Act in2000 and
    certified in January 2001.



Note: The individual project reports summarise the findings of the Review Team
regarding materiai compliance issues, and present project specific recommendationsfor
the consideration of the Interagency Forestry Review Committee. Separate reports
produced at the end of the review process set out in more detail the audit procedures
applied, and comments and recommenaations regaraing existing policies, legal
requirements and project development processes.

  A. FORESTRY AND PLANNING ASPECTS

  The clearing of forested land for roading development does not require the application of
  the same sectoral planning and control measures as are required for long term
  sustainable forestry projects under the National Forest Policy 1991, the Forestry Act
  1999 and the National Forestry Guidelines 1993. The key issues for road line clearing
  Timber Authorities are:

      To ensure that the proposed roading development is consistent with the National or
      Provincialtransport plans; that the funds for road constructionare available and have
      been committed; and that responsibility for road maintenance is cieariy defined and
      accepted;
      -  zflsc:? t-3:          ;!e :--e      *:-?   -=. lcrest is undertaken in a progressive manner
                                                       6-
      in accordancewith the road CC;;~::       ,;:;on    programme, thus protectingas much of the
      forest as is possible against the potential non-performanceof the roading contractor,
      and

      That the road line clearing and road construction is undertakenin an environmentally
      responsible manner.

  In this case the Timber Authority was allegedly issued in April 1994 before detailed
  procedures and requirements for Timber Authorities were developed. These
  -=xirements were developed during 1995, and recognisedthat the timber revenue from

  Review of `In Process" Forestry Projects
  Individual Project Report 31 -Aiambak-Kiunga             Road TA                            Page 1

     a road line clearing operation would not meet the cost of road construction unless
I    logging of a much wider corridor was allowed. A maximum road line clearance of 40 m
     was imposed and supported by a National Executive Council decision (113/96). To be
     compliantwith the Act, any logging outside of this 40 m road line must be under either a
     Forest ManagementAgreement, or a Timber Harvesting Timber Authority.

     The Timber Authority procedures and requirements developed by the PNGFA also
     required observance of environmental standards which for roading constructionwere set
     out in the PNG Logging Code of practice 1996.

     The Aiambak-Kiunga Road TA does not meet the current requirements of the Act in two
     key aspects:

         It allows logging outside of the 40 m wide road line without a Forest Management
        Agreement or a Timber Harvesting Timber Authority. The original Timber Authority
        document provides that "harvesting [may take place on] both sides of the proposed
        road alignment". The Logging and Marketing Agreement between the TA holder
        (Paiso Company Pty Ltd) and the logger (Concord Pacific Pty Ltd) is more specific in
        that it provides for logging a forest corridor up to 2 km in width, and the hawesting of
        4,200 m3 of logs for every kilometre of road constructed (or a total of 1.0 million m3
        of logs for the 246 km Icng rcad).

     0  It does not require full observance of the environmentai standards for roadingset out
        in the PNG Logging Code of Practice 1996. The TA dccument provides for some
        rudimentaryobservance of environmentalconcerns by requiringthe holder to "avoid"
        certain specified impacts. Howeverthese obligations are not clearly passedon to the
        loggerin the Logging and MarketingAgreement.

    The roading standard specified in the Logging and Marketing Agreement is a "dry
    weather 4x4"road. A road of this type in this wet part of PNG is unlikely to be usable for
    any significant periods, or to last long without significant expenditure on road
    maintenance. It is difficult to see the demand which would justify this type of road.
    Generally this project is seen as a thinly disguised method employed by a logging
    company to gain access to logs for export.

    RECOMMENDATIONSREGARDING FORESTRY ASPECTS:

    1. That any application to extend the scope and term of this Timber Authority be
        soundly rejected.

    2. That any fP%?      xplicaticn for rcad licz :. :::3g  be subjected to the requirementof
        the Act as amended.


    B LEGAL COMPLIANCE
      .
    SUMMARYOF LEGALCOMPLIANCE:

    Since Minister Neville purported to approve TA No 24 in April 1994 no procedural step
    under the ForestryAct 1991 has been duly observed. In giving his approvalthe Minister


    Review of YnProcess" Forestry Projects
    IndividualProject Report 31   -Aiambak-Kiunga     Road TA                           Page2

exceeded his powers. Under the Act Ministers have no procedural role to play in relation
to Timber Authorities.

TA No 24 was signed by the Regional Forestry Inspector "as a delegate of the Board".
Under the Act it was the Provincial Forest Minister at that time who was empoweredto
grant a Timber Authority. However the Act prescribes a lengthy procedureto be followed
before such a grant can be made. That procedure was completely overlooked in relation
to this project.

The subsequent decisions by Acting Minister Philemon and Minister Pok to grant
extensions to TA No 24 are also not supported by provisions of the Act. The Act states
that TimberAuthorities are to be valid for the stated period and makes no mentionof any
power to extend them. It seems that a new application must be made when a Timber
Authority expires. In any event there is no provision made at all for any power to be
exercised by the National Ministerfor Forests.

Logging operations are proceeding on the basis of a far-reaching Court Order made on
26 November 1999. This Order permits :he operations to continue under TA No 24 and
restrainsthe PNGFAfrom seizing logs or delaying export permits.

The current Managing Cirector and PNGFA staff have demcnstrated a clear
determipaticn tc $39thrt ccme ccr!;sis ars 5xerz:sed cver trrs remaxhcie 7rzjec:. T;er
attempts to apply the provisions of the Act have Deen thwarted at every stage. The
senous ramifications of the propct affecting the rights of landowners and the good
governance of this country cannot be attnbuted to the current staff of the PNGFA in any
way.

NEC Submission 73/2000 (9 May 2000) seeks, inter alia, the approval of the NEC for a
15 year extension to TA No 24. The Submission suggests that there are no legislative
implications. This is incorrect and NEC should be aware that the Submission effectively
invites Cabinet to breach the statutory procedures that are prescribed in the Forestry
Act.

RECOMMENDATIONS REGARDING LEGAL ASPECTS:

1. That the court proceedings must be brought to a conclusion. The substantive issues
    must be finaily determined. It should be noted that the Attorney General has
    previously acted in a private capacity for the logging operator (Concorde Pacific Ltd)
    in relationto these proceedings.

<,t-`jtic-zl > ! y A + * -*-= \Ise?    ' = . a - 7 `-:T]Farum ;;as mted :hat logsing activity has
continued despire ;.xrxcT;;mcc.z:;ms of the Review Team. A key proponent of this
project was deported from Papua New Guinea for a short period, but now seems to
enjoy citizenship status by virtue of a court order. This project has becomecharacterised
by the interventionof a court to permit its ccnnnuzrion.

                         PNG FORESTRY REVIEW TEAM

         AUDITING FORESTRY PROJECTS CURRENTLY "IN PROCESS" FOR
 COMPLIANCE WITH THEREQUIREMENTS OF THE POLICY, THEFORESTRY ACT
                     AND OTHER REGULATIONS AND GUIDEUNES


 To:                    Government of Papua New Guinea
                        C/- The Interagency Forestry Review Committee
                        Office of the Chief Secretav to Government

 From:                  ReviewTeam

 Date:                  4 October 2001 (Updated draft of 5 Marcn 2001)

 Re:                    INDIVIDUAL PROJECT REVIEW REPORT NUMBER24

                        POND0 (EAST NEW BRITAIN PROVINCE)



AUDIT CONCLUSIONS AND RECOMMENDATIONS:

RESOURCEAND PLANNING ISSUES:

The sustainable timber yield prrnciole has not been compiied with (as a consequence of
the resource being very small). The TRP either has expired or will expire soon. The
project is not in compliance with the Act in that it is not listed in the NationalForest Plan
for development. Sensible operational procedures have not been complied with in that
there has been no field volumetric inventory. The gross loggable area and estimated
loggable volume appear to be significantly overstated. The estimatedsustainableannual
cut is insufficientto support either a financially efficient logging project or a conventional
stand alone log export project. In the absence of a Forest ManagementAgreementthere
is no provision for 10% of the gross loggable area to be set aside for conservation
purposes. It may be sensible to conserve this resource for domestic sawn timber supply
for this heavily logged province.

LEGALCOMPLIANCE:

The failure to base this project on a Forest Management Agreement is a breach of due
process. There is no sense in gra'nting this project as an extension to the Seraji
ExtensionTRP as that TRP expires in early 2002.

LANDOWNER ISSUES:

There is no certainty that the landowners of the Pondo TRP area are the same as the
Seraji TRP as asserted by the PNGFA         - the clan lists do not match. There are no
indications of landowner concems having been considered in the DevelopmentOptions
Study.

Review of "InProcess"Forestry Projects
Individual Project Report 24 Pondo

      RECOMMENDATIONS(INCLUDING CORRECTIVE MEASURES IF REQUIRED):

         That this project should not proceed in its current form without a Forest Management
         Agreement.

     0   That the idea of granting this project as an extension to the Seraji and Seraji
         Extensionproject should be abandoned.

     9   That consideration be given to proceeding in due course on the basis of a Timber
         Authority to support domestic sawn timber supply.



     Note: The individual project reports summarise the findings of the Review Team
     regarding materiai compliance issues, and present project specific recommendationsfor
     the consideration of the Interagency Forestry Review Committee. Separate reports

     applied, and comments and recommendations regarding existing policies, legal
     requirements and projectdevelopment processes.




1    Addendum:

     Since the preparation of the first draft of this report in March 2001, despite advice from
     the National Forest Service, the PNG Forest Authority Managing Director issued
     permissionto a logging company to "set up base camp and construct advance roading"
     in the Pondo TRP area. This was illegal as there was neither a Timber Permit or a
     Timber Authority through which any rights could be given. Inaddition the permissionwas
     in direct breach of the Govemment's current moratorium on the issuance of logging
     permits.

     The Managing Director later revoked his permission, and his action was duly noted by
     the Board. In the interim some 8,500 m3 of logs with a value of Kina 1.4 million were
     exported'.

CHECKLISTNOTES:

1.     Tne fires inaicate a poor use oi prescribed Forms.

2.     The PNGFA Board Minutes suggest that the Board has exercised no authority in
        relation to this project. This indicates that nothing has been done to keep the
       NFB advised of its progress. The only reference to this project in the Board
       Minutes is at Meeting 17 in March 1995 when it was resolved that the project
       would be "expedited". It cannot be said that this was achieved.

3.     This project purports to be based on a former TRP. There is no evidence on the
       files to indicate that it has been guiaed by any clear legal advice. It has been
       suggested in the notes to the Rai Coast project (Individual Forestry Review
       Report No 23) that proceeding on the basis of former TRPs may be misguided.
       This is becausethe essential eiements of the new system, Le. the replacementof
       landowner companies with ILGs and the apolication of principles of sustainable
       management,will be avoided. It is suggested in those notes that TRPs are saved
       under section 137 to avoid a wholesaie exringuishment of the contractual rights
       that they create, and not for them to replace the FMA procedure as a basis for
       projectsthat are not in operational mode.

4.     In this case however, there are particular reasons why the project cannot be
       basedupon the TRP. They include      -
           The TRP may not in fact be saved by section 137. The date of the TRP is not
           certain but it appears to be some time in 1941 or 1945. Section 137 only
           saves TRPs that were "granted" under the Forestry Act (Chapter 216). This
           TRP must have been granted under a former colonial Ordinance.

           Even if the TRP was saved, then it appears that it may have expired in 2001
           (if it was purchased on 26 March 1941 as suggested by the Assistant
           Secretary in a letter dated 24 January 1989), or that it will expire in 2005 (if
           the PFMC was correct in ascribing that year as its final year in Decision
           5/2000 at Meeting 2/2000 held on 22 June 2000). Eitherway it indicates that
           the TRP is an entirely inappropriate basisfor this project.

           No copy of the TRP seems to exist. If it was signed in 1941 then it probably
           did not survive the Japanese invasion of Rabaul. If it was signed in 1945,
           which seems unlikely, thenit may not have survived the more recent infemo
           at PNGFA headquarters. In either event it should regarded as of no effect
           and a proper procedure under the current Act should be applied. As the
           annual allowable cut would only be 500 cubic metres more than that which
           would be permissibleunder a Timber Authority then that procedure remainsa
           realisticalternative to a FMA.




Review of "InProcess"ForestryPrcjects
Individual ProjectReport 24 Pondo                                                  Page2

     5.    The notion of granting the project as an extension to the Seraji operations is also
            misguided for similar reasons. The Seraji Extension TRP is for a term of 20 years
1           commencing 1 January 1982. It has only 11 months to run and therefore should
            not be consideredas a basis for the proposed operation of the Pondo project as
           an extension. The application submitted by the adjoining permit holdershould not
            be entertained.

    6.     There is another matter of concern that should be noted also. The landowner
           company holding the Timber Permit unaer the Seraji Extension TRP, Nangal
           Limited, had experienced troubles with its contractor. Deegold. The contractor
           walked off the project in early 1998 and then sometime later attemptedto re-start
           operations. Deegold decided to avoid further confrontation with the resource
           owners by suggesting that they would agree to terminate their Logging and
           MarketingAgreement if a new Agreement was signed with Everwell Limited. The
           landowners appear to have accepted this and sought approval for the new
           Agreement in 1999. It should not come as a surprise that Deegold and Everwell
           are, for all intents and purposes, the same. The details of registration for both
           companies are identical. Yii Ann Hii is recorded as the sole shareholder of both.
           Nancy Seo and Joyce Lee are directors of both, and in both companies hold the
           designation of Financial Controller and General Manager respectively.Addresses
           and telephone numbers for both companies are identical. Somebody seems to
           have pulled somerhing cver scmebody else's eyes.

    7.     The NGOs Eco-Forestry Forum and PNG Forest Watch have both referred to
           rscent logging in the Pondo TRP area, presumabiy by the operator in the
           adjoining Seraji Extension TRP. This illegal logging activity has been confirmed
           :o have taken place. It appears that about 9,500 m3 cf logs have been cut, and
           that mcst of this has been exporred. Notwithstandingthat the approval may have
           been given only to enable road construction to the area, this appears to be a
           serious breach of the Act and the Moratorium. The files indicatethat a number of
           NFS officers properly counselled against giving any permission to log in the area.
           This advice followed a direction by the Minister on 8"' May 2001 to the NFS "to
           prepare the necessary documents for my signature to allocate Pondo TRP to
           Nangal Ltd". The Managing Director had aiso sought advice on 20'" April 2001
           and indicated that he was willing to "bend the rules". He indicated a desire to
           "fasttrack this project for the benefit of the landowners".

           Notwithstanding that as much as 9,500 m3 of logs may have been harvested
           illegally, it should be noted that the NFS firmly advocated observance of due
           process, and that the PNGFA Board subsequently intervened to uphold the
           requirementsof the Act.

                       PNG FORESTRY REVIEW TEAM

        AUDITING FORESTRY PROJECTS CURRENTLY "IN PROCESS"FOR
 COMPLIANCE WITH THEREQUIREMENTS OF THE POLICY, THEFORESTRYACT
                   AND OTHER REGULATIONSAND GUIDELINES


To:                   Government of Paoua New Guinea
                      C/- The Interagency Forestry Review Committee
                      Office oi the Chief Secretary to Government

From:                 ReviewTeam

Date:                 4 October 2001 (Updated draft of 5 March 2001)

Re:                   INDIVIDUALPROJECTREVIEW REPORTNUMBER27

                      TUWAPU (WEST SEPIK)



AUDIT CONCLUSIONS AND RECOMMENDATIONS:

RESOURCEAND PLANNING ISSUES:

The sustainable timber yield principle has been complied with. The project is not in
compliance with the Act in that it is not listed in the National Forest Plan for
development. The gross loggable area has been significantly overestimated in the
Forest ManagementAgreement (most of the area has already been logged) resultingin
high landowner expectations. The estimated net loggable volume is not sufficient to
support a practical sustainable annual cut, and thus falls outside the intent of the
National ForestPolicy. The project is being progressedas if it will be an extensionfor TP
10-08Vanimo, but there is no indication that the permit holder has expressed any direct
interest. PNGFA staff are aware that this project is far too small to support a sustainable
cut, but it would appear that management has failed to exercise its decision making
authority by sensibly rejecting the project as a viable Forest Management Agreement
opportunity.

LEGALCOMPLIANCE:

%e piscass tias yerxraiiy been ioiiowea. Tine usual concerns aoout PFMC certification
of the forest ManagementAgreement are indicated here. There are defects in the form
of the Forest Management Agreement. The assumption that the project is an extension
is unfoundeduntilan application is duly made and approved by the Board.

LANDOWNER ISSUES:

Landownershave been involvedwith logging operations by Vanimo Timber Products Ltd
for a generation. Uncertainty within the PNGFA as to how to handle this small area has

Review of "InProcess" Forestry Projects
IndividualProject Report 24 Pondo

resulted in the inappropriate execution of a Forest Management Agreement over their
(mostly)logged land creating confusion and unrealisticexpectations.

RECOMMENDATIONS(INCLUDINGCORRECTIVE MEASURES IF REQUIRED):

That beforethe project is allowed to proceed any further, that:

    The PNGFA re-assess the net loggable volume, taking care that areas already
    logged are not logged a second time, and reviews the sensibility of progressingthis
    project under a Forest ManagementAgreement.

    That the PNGFA informs landowners of the limited size of the loggable resource.

    The PNGFA ascertain the interest of Vanimo Forest Products Ltd in logging the (re-
    assessed) resource as an extension of TP 10-08 given the recent amendments to
    the Act.

IfVanimo Forest Products Ltd is not interested, then:

    That the Forest ManagementAgreement be cancelled.

If for any reason the project is to proceed under the Forest Management Agreement
then:

    That the defects in the agreement must be remedied.

    That the PFMC certification might be revisited.

    That the project should not be considered as an extension until the Board has made
    a resolutionto this effect, taking into account the recent amendments to the Act.



Note: The individual project reports summarise the findings of the Review Team
regarding material compliance issues, and present project specific recommendationsfor
the consideration of the Interagency Forestry Review Committee. Separate reports
produced at the end of the review process set out in more detail the audit procedures
applied, and comments and recommendations regarding existing policies, legal
requirementsand projectdevelopment processes.



Addendum:

Since the preparationof the first drat3 of this report in March 2001, despite advice from
the National Forest Service, the PNG Forest Authority Managing Director issued
permissionto undertake logging in the Tuwapu TRP area. This was illegal as there was
neither a Timber Permit or a Timber Authority through which any rights could be given.
In addition the permission was in direct breach of the Government's cment "atOnUm
on the issuanceof loggingpermits.

B LEGAL COMPLIANCE
   .
SUMMARY OF LEGAL COMPLIANCE:

    Due process appears to have been generally followed, but there is insufficient
    documentationto verify this at every stage. Doubts exist as to the PFMC certification
    of the Forest Management Agreement. There are defects in the form of the Forest
    ManagementAgreement.

    The assumption that the project will be an extension to the nearby Vanimo Forest
    Productsoperations is unfoundedat this time. No formal applicationhas been lodged
    by the company, but there are some indications that landownersmight be being used
    to securethe company's position in ways that are not consistentwith the Act.

    The DevelopmentOptions Study seems to be satisfactory.

A full checklist and accompanying notes are presented in Appendix 1.

RECOMMENDATIONS REGARDING LEGAL ASPECTS:

If a decision is made to further progress this project under a Forest Management
Agreement, then:

1. That the PFMC certificationof the Forest Management Agreement should be verified
    and rectified if necessary.

2. That the defects in the form of the Forest Management Agreement must be
    addressed.

3. Inat consultations with resource owners and the Provincial Government must take
    -.
    place before the ProjectGuidelinesare finalised.

4. That the project must not be considered as an extension to the Vanimo TRP project
    until the Board has formally and properly made such a decision in accordance with
    the recent (December 2000) amendmentsto the Act.

CHECKL!ST NOTES:

1.      The usual concerns about the PFMC certification of FMAs apply here. There is
        no evidence that landowner representatives were in attendance at the PFMC
        meeting. And there is no confirmation that the PFMC sought to independently
        verify the incorporation of the sole ILG or the willingness of that ILG to sign the
        FMA.

        Indeed there is a suggestion on the files that the process of certification was
        done in a very cavaiierfashion. On 3 May 1999the ManagerAcquisitions wrote a
        Minute to the Provincial Forest Officer directing that he arrange the Chairman of
        the PFMC to sign the certificate in Schedule 6 to the FMA. Three days later this
       was signed. The correct request was.for the PFMC to meet and to perform its
       statutory function. One is left to hope that this had beendone properly, but there
        is nothing on the PNGFAfiles to indicate this.

2.     There are defects in the form of the FMA. It is not dated and the importantdetails
        have not Seen insened into Schedule 1.

3.     The DOS was done satisfactorily and gives some details of the development
       aspirations of the landowners.A copy of the draft ProjectGuidelines was sighted.

4.      It S S ~ E S;3 22 SSS-i*:ez 2; Z,i t:st tze crc!EC: W C ! ~ oe giver; 2s ZI? eXIEcSi2n IC
       the adjacent area in which Vanimo Forests Products Ltd operates. In mid-1999
       Vanimo Forest Products seems to have attempted to obtain some right to
       operate by making application for a Licence on Form 177. This was an entirely
       inappropriate appiication to make, and was properly returned by the Managing
       Director on 14 July 1999. Soon after that there are a number of letters from a
       landowner company, which had not been involvedin the project before that time,
       endorsing VFP and asking for the processes to be short-circuited. IfVFP had any
       part in this then its activities must again be seen as inappropriate. Interestingly,
       VFP appears to have never formally applied for the Board to approve the project
       as an extension. It may be that they favoured encouraging landownersto speak
       for them. Until an application is made and approved by the Board, there are no
       grounds upon which a presumption can be made that the project will be an
       extension.

5.     There are reasons to think that the advice offered by the Acting Divisional
       Manager      -Forest Planning on 22 January 2000 is sound. His suggestionwas for
       the `FMA (to) remain intact and the developer to extend its operations into the
       FMA area but through the normal allocation process". Howeverit is up to VFP to
       pursue the normal process and not become involved in questionableattempts to
       by-pass it.

6.     The NGO Eco-Forestry Forum has referred to logging activitytaking place in the
       Tuwapu FMA area. File records confirm that this activity has taken place. This
       appears to be based upon a decision by the Managing Director to ignore the

Review of Yn Process"Forestry Projects
Individual Project Report 27 Tuwapu                                                      Page 2

        FMA and to include Tuwapu as part of Block 6 of the adjacent Vanimo TRP.
        Vanimo ForestProductsLtd's loggingplanwas approvedon 7* May 2001.

        On 18 January 2001 the Manging Director was advised by the PNGFA General
        Counsel that Tuwapu did not fall into the Vanimo TRP. He was specifically
        advised that 'the FMA remains in place and is not part of the TRP area". This
        observation was supported by a note written on the advice of another NFS
        officer. It is clear from the boundary description in the Vanimo TRP document
        and the Timber Permit that the Tuwapu FMA area was never acquired as part of
        the Vanimo TRP.

        The decision to allow logging seems to be a serious breach of the Act and the
        moratorium.

                                       TheLoan

       Section 2.01. The Bank agrees to lend to the Borrower, on the terms and
 conditions set forth or referred to in this Agreement, an amount equal to seventeen
 million three hundredsixty thousand Dollars (%17,360,000), as such amount may be
 converted from time to time through a Currency Conversioninaccordance with the
 provisions of Section2.09 ofthis Agreement.

       Section 2.02. (a) The amount of the Loan may be withdrawn h m the Loan
 Account in accordance with the provisions of Schedule 1 to this Agreement for
 expenditures made (or, if the Bank shall so agree, to be made) in respect of the
reasonable cost of works, goods and services required for Parts A, C and D of the
Projectand to be financed out of the proceedsof the Loanand inrespect of the hnt-
endfee referredto inSection2.04ofthis Agreement.

         (b) The Borrower may, for the purposesof Parts A, C andDof the Project
open and maintain in Kina a special deposit account ina commercia1bank on terms
and conditions satisfactory to the Bank, including appropriateprotection against set-
off, seizure andattachment. Deposits into, andpayments out of, the SpecialAccount
shall bemade inaccordance with the provisionsof Schedule 6 to thss Agreement.

         Section 2.03. The Closing Date shall be June 30,2008, or such later date as
the Bank shall establish. The Bank shall promptly no@ the Borrower of such later
date.

         Section 2.04. The Borrower shall pay to the Bank a hnt-end fee in an
amount equal to one percent (1%) o f the amount of the Loan. The Borrower agrees
that on or promptly after the Effective Date, the Bank shall, on behalf of the
Borrower, withdraw h mthe LoanAccount andpayto itself the amount of such fee.

         Section 2.05. The Borrower shallpay to the Bank a commitment charge on
the principal amount of the Loannot withdrawn h m time to time, at a rate equal to:
(i)eightyfiveone-hundredthsofonepercent(0.85%) perannumh mthedateon
which suchchargecommences to acme inaccordancewiththe provisions of Section
3.02 of the General Conditions to but not including the fourth anniversary of such
date; and (ii)seventy five one-hundredths of one per cent (0.75%) per m u m
thereafter.

         Section 2.06. The Borrower shall pay interest on the principalamount of the
Loan withdrawn andoutstandingh mtime to time, inrespect of each InterestPeriod
at the Variable Rate; provided, that upon a Conversion of all or any portion of the
principal amount of the Loan, the Borrower shall, during the ConversionPeriod, pay
interest on such amount inaccordance with the relevant provisions o f Article IV of
the GeneralConditions.

                                    SCHEDULE2

                              Descriptionof the Project

          The objective of the Project is to assist the Borrower to improve sustainable

(a) enhanced processes for landowner participation in forest management and
 forest resourcemanagementinThe Independent State of PapuaNew Guinea, through

conservation, @) provision of financing to implement forest management options
consistent with forest biodiversity conservation, (c) streamlined planning, monitoring
and enforcement capacity of the PNG Forest Authority, and (a) strengthened

EnvironmentandConservation
environmental impact assessment wd monitoring capabilities of the           Office af


         The Project consists of the following parts, subject to such modifications
thereof as the Borrower and the Bank may agree upon from time to time to achieve
suchobjectives:

PartA: Landowner ForestDecision-Making

1.     Develop and implement processes to enhance forest landowners participation
in forest managementand conservation, including educational activities to improve
landowner access to information, and improved institutional and legal arrangements
for organizing landowner representation, regarding forest management and
conservation, and provision of technical and financial assistance to implement their
chosenforest developmentoption.

2.     Develop andimplementConservationManagementAreas through the adoption
o f policies and enactment of legislation for comunity-initiated conservation and
sustainableresourcemanagementareason customaryland.

PartB: PNGMamab u nConservationTrust Fund

1.     Implementation by Beneficiaries of specific forest biodiversity consemation
and sustainable projects, including the provision of Grants and Sub-grants and
technical assistance therefor.

2.    Develop and implement the PNG Mama Gram Conservation Trust Fund,
including provision of technical assistance, office facilities, office equipment and
vehicles therefor.

PartC: SustainableForestManagement

1.    Enhance the PNG Forest Authority's capability to manage, plan, implement
and monitor sustainable forest operations, including the provision of PNGFA staff

                                          - 18-


training and workshops, field and ofice equipment, vehicles, computers         and
consultants' services.

2.     Improvement o f naturaI production forest management though expansion of
sustained yield post harvest activities, including the provision o f PNGFA staff
training andworkshops, field andoffice facilities andequipment, vehicles, computers
andconsultants' services.

3.     Development o f post b e s t management activities andfeasibility studies fix
development of plantations on degraded forest Iands, including feasibility studies,
development of a f o ~ s tplantation smtegy and testing of metfiod4logyon a pilot
basis.
-
PartD: Environmental AssessmentandMonitoring

1.     Development, testing andimplementing environmental impact assessmentsand
monitoring methodologies, including development of operational manuals, OEC staff
trainingandworkshops, field andoffice facilities andequipmen4 vehicles, computers
andconsultants' services.

2.     Designing and implementing a community-based environmental monitoring
program, including training to trainers within govemment agencies and Non-
Governmental Organizations established inPNG, and testing the approach inseveral
pilot areas.

                                          * * *

            The Project is expected to be completedbyDecember 31,2007.

arrangements satisfactory to the Bank. To assist PNGFA inthis undertaking, PNGFA
shall employ andretain consultantswith qualifications, terms of referenceand tenns
andconditions ofemploymentsatisfactoryto the Bank, untiltheBorrowerestablishes
and maintains a Probity Commissioner to carry out forest resource allocation
processes under the Project, on terms and conditions satisfactoryto the Bank. These
consultants shall be retained inaccordance withthe provisions set forth inSectionII,
Part B o f Schedule 4 to this Agreement. For purposes of this paragraph the term
"logging permits" means Forest Management Agreements, Timber Permits, Timber
Authorities andgeographic extensions to Timber Permits.

           26 JUNE2000


1  From:     "greenpeace"<gpacific@dg.com.pg>on 06/26/2000 11:23PMZElO
   To:       "Klaus Rohland"<Krohland@worldbank.org>
   cc:       "World Bank POM" <wbpng@datec.com.pg>,"JamesDouglas"<jdouglas@worldbank.org>
   bcc:
   Subject: papua new guinea:log moratorium


   There is a very serious discrepancy betweenwhat was agreedto betweenthe
   Bank and the NGOsover the log moratorium,and what the GofPNG has signed up
   to.

   What we thought the Bank was supportingwas a moratoriumon all new logging
   projects, until there has been a compete review of all existing concessions.
   A report in todays PNG Post Courier (Skatetabled in Parliamentthe 19
   conditions set by the World Bank) seems to bear this out (seeannexureA).

   But we now know that the Submissionby the Ministerfor Foreststo the NEC
   on the moratoriumasked for a moratoriumwhile only the Skate Government new
   fast-track projectswere evaluated (annexureB).

   And the NEC agreed with that (annexureC).

   This is not good enough, becausethe reasonwe needed a moratoriumwhile
   existing projectswere evaluatedwas becauseof the high levels of
   non-complianceby existing operators.

   It simply makes no sense to evaluatethe processof concession acquisition,
   when the issue is industry non-compliance.A review of the allocation
1  processof the fast-tracked projects does not addressthe issueof
   non-compliance.Already Chris Marlowe, GeneralCounselof the PNGFA is
   allegedto have indicatedthat the reviewof the allocation process is a
   technical matter that could be completedin a few days by his staff.

   Meanwhilethe PNG ForestAuthority is ignoringboth the spirit and the terms
   of the moratorium.It is quite clear from the NEC decisionthat it applies
   to all processes(FMA acquisition and timber permit issuing).The PNG FA has
   called for tenders on two concessions since the moratoriumcame into
   effect. Semabo, Western Province.This concession is too smallto be
   sustanable, and is 65% subject to inundation.The previouspermit holder
   turned the permitin becauseit was uneconomical.



   They have also advertisedAmanab blocks 1to 4 in the Sandaun Province. The
   PNGFA is probablytrying to drive the process so far that it will create
   contractualrelations (as it did with Vailala Block 3) and lock the
   Government into a an agreement by virtue of the threat of court awarded
   damages. The applicants for these concessions include Damansera,RH and WTK,
   companieswith an established record of non compliance.

   1. Canwe have some comfortthat the Bankwill ensurethat the moratorium
   stays in place until there has been an indepedemtand transparent evaluation
   of existing concessions?

   2. will the Bank undertaketo fund a full-scale review of existing
   projects?

   Brian Brunton
